				<div class="minerva__subtitle"><span class="mw-redirectedfrom">&#160;&#160;(Redirected from <a href="/w/index.php?title=Costco_Wholesale_Corp.&amp;redirect=no" class="mw-redirect" title="Costco Wholesale Corp.">Costco Wholesale Corp.</a>)</span></div>
			</div>
			
			<div id="bodyContent" class="content"><div id="mw-content-text" lang="en" dir="ltr" class="mw-content-ltr"><script>function mfTempOpenSection(id){var block=document.getElementById("mf-section-"+id);block.className+=" open-block";block.previousSibling.className+=" open-block";}</script><div class="mw-parser-output"><section class="mf-section-0" id="mf-section-0"><div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Not to be confused with <a href="/wiki/COSCO" title="COSCO">COSCO</a>, <a href="/wiki/Cosco_(India)_Limited" title="Cosco (India) Limited">Cosco (India) Limited</a>, <a href="/wiki/Cusco" title="Cusco">Cusco</a>, or <a href="/wiki/CUSCO_Japan" title="CUSCO Japan">CUSCO Japan</a>.</div>
<p><b>Costco Wholesale Corporation</b>, <a href="/wiki/Trade_name" title="Trade name">doing business as</a> <b>Costco</b>, is an American <a href="/wiki/Multinational_corporation" title="Multinational corporation">multinational corporation</a> which operates a chain of membership-only <a href="/wiki/Warehouse_club" title="Warehouse club">warehouse clubs</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-2">[2]</a></sup> As of 2015<sup class="plainlinks noexcerpt noprint asof-tag update" style="display:none;"><a class="external text" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Costco&amp;action=edit">[update]</a></sup>, Costco was the <a href="/wiki/Retail#Global_top_ten_retailers" title="Retail">second largest retailer in the world</a> after <a href="/wiki/Walmart" title="Walmart">Walmart</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-3">[3]</a></sup> and as of 2016<sup class="plainlinks noexcerpt noprint asof-tag update" style="display:none;"><a class="external text" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Costco&amp;action=edit">[update]</a></sup>, Costco was the world's largest retailer of <a href="/wiki/Beef_carcass_classification" title="Beef carcass classification">choice and prime beef</a>, <a href="/wiki/Organic_foods" class="mw-redirect" title="Organic foods">organic foods</a>, <a href="/wiki/Rotisserie_chicken" title="Rotisserie chicken">rotisserie chicken</a>, and wine.<sup id="cite_ref-Gabler_4-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Gabler-4">[4]</a></sup> As of 2019<sup class="plainlinks noexcerpt noprint asof-tag update" style="display:none;"><a class="external text" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Costco&amp;action=edit">[update]</a></sup>, Costco is ranked #14 on the <a href="/wiki/Fortune_500" title="Fortune 500">Fortune 500</a> rankings of the largest United States corporations by total revenue.<sup id="cite_ref-Fortune_500_5-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Fortune_500-5">[5]</a></sup></p><table class="infobox vcard" height="45" class="thumbimage" data-file-width="1119" data-file-height="229"></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Costco%27s_original_logo_2010-01-16.png" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Costco's original logo. Used until 1993, but stores continued to carry the logo until 1997.</div></div></div>
<p>Costco's worldwide headquarters are in <a href="/wiki/Issaquah,_Washington" title="Issaquah, Washington">Issaquah, Washington</a>, a suburb east of <a href="/wiki/Seattle" title="Seattle">Seattle</a>; the company opened its first warehouse (the chain's term for its retail outlets) in Seattle 37 years ago <span class="nowrap">in 1983.<sup id="cite_ref-spoketh_6-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-spoketh-6">[6]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-7" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-7">[7]</a></sup></span> Through mergers, Costco's corporate history dates back to 1976, when its former competitor <a href="/wiki/Price_Club" title="Price Club">Price Club</a> was founded in <a href="/wiki/San_Diego,_California" class="mw-redirect" title="San Diego, California">San Diego, California</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-8" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-8">[8]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-membership_9-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-membership-9">[9]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-highlights_10-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-highlights-10">[10]</a></sup> As of December 31, 2019<sup class="plainlinks noexcerpt noprint asof-tag update" style="display:none;"><a class="external text" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Costco&amp;action=edit">[update]</a></sup>, Costco has a total of 785 warehouses:<sup id="cite_ref-2019_Annual_Report_1-8" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-2019_Annual_Report-1">[1]</a></sup> 546 in the United States and Puerto Rico, 100 in Canada, 39 in Mexico, 29 in the United Kingdom, 26 in Japan, 16 in South Korea, 14 in Taiwan, 11 in Australia, two in Spain, one in Iceland, one in France, and one in China.<sup id="cite_ref-2019_Annual_Report_1-9" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-2019_Annual_Report-1">[1]</a></sup> Costco is scheduled to open a warehouse in New Zealand in 2021.<sup id="cite_ref-11" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-11">[11]</a></sup></p>

</section><h2 class="section-heading" onclick="javascript:mfTempOpenSection(1)"><div class="mw-ui-icon mw-ui-icon-element indicator mw-ui-icon-small mw-ui-icon-flush-left"></div><span class="mw-headline" id="History">History</span><span class="mw-editsection"><a href="/w/index.php?title=Costco&amp;action=edit&amp;section=1" title="Edit section: History" data-section="1" class="mw-ui-icon mw-ui-icon-element mw-ui-icon-wikimedia-edit-base20 edit-page mw-ui-icon-flush-right">Edit</a></span></h2><section class="mf-section-1 collapsible-block" id="mf-section-1">

<h3 class="in-block"><span class="mw-headline" id="Price_Club_and_the_birth_of_the_retail_warehouse_concept">Price Club and the birth of the retail warehouse concept</span><span class="mw-editsection"><a href="/w/index.php?title=Costco&amp;action=edit&amp;section=2" title="Edit section: Price Club and the birth of the retail warehouse concept" data-section="2" class="mw-ui-icon mw-ui-icon-element mw-ui-icon-wikimedia-edit-base20 edit-page mw-ui-icon-flush-right">Edit</a></span></h3>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Price_Club" title="Price Club">Price Club</a></div>
<p>Costco's history began with <a href="/wiki/Sol_Price" title="Sol Price">Sol Price</a> and his son, Robert, opening the first Price Club warehouse on July 12, 1976, on Morena Boulevard in San Diego, California, thus giving birth to a new concept: a retail warehouse club. The Price family placed Price Club Warehouse <abbr title="Number">#</abbr>1 inside a series of old airplane hangars<sup id="cite_ref-membership_9-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-membership-9">[9]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-highlights_10-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-highlights-10">[10]</a></sup> previously owned by <a href="/wiki/Howard_Hughes" title="Howard Hughes">Howard Hughes</a>; that warehouse, now known as Costco Warehouse #401, is still in operation today.<sup id="cite_ref-12" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-12">[12]</a></sup></p>
<h3 class="in-block"><span class="mw-headline" id="Costco_opens">Costco opens</span><span class="mw-editsection"><a href="/w/index.php?title=Costco&amp;action=edit&amp;section=3" title="Edit section: Costco opens" data-section="3" class="mw-ui-icon mw-ui-icon-element mw-ui-icon-wikimedia-edit-base20 edit-page mw-ui-icon-flush-right">Edit</a></span></h3>
<p>Costco opened its first warehouse in 1983 in Seattle on <span class="nowrap">September 15,<sup id="cite_ref-membership_9-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-membership-9">[9]</a></sup></span> by <a href="/wiki/James_Sinegal" title="James Sinegal">James (Jim) Sinegal</a> and <a href="/wiki/Jeffrey_Brotman" title="Jeffrey Brotman">Jeffrey H. Brotman</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-13" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-13">[13]</a></sup> Sinegal had started in wholesale distribution by working for Sol Price at <a href="/wiki/FedMart" title="FedMart">FedMart</a>; Brotman, an <a href="/wiki/Attorney_at_law_(United_States)" class="mw-redirect" title="Attorney at law (United States)">attorney</a> from an old Seattle retailing family, had also been involved in retail distribution from an early age. He began his retail involvement as a <a href="/wiki/Bagger" title="Bagger">grocery bagger</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-14" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-14">[14]</a></sup> A second store opened in <a href="/wiki/Portland,_Oregon" title="Portland, Oregon">Portland</a> in October, and a third in <a href="/wiki/Spokane,_Washington" title="Spokane, Washington">Spokane</a> in <span class="nowrap">December 1983.<sup id="cite_ref-spoketh_6-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-spoketh-6">[6]</a></sup></span>
</p>
<h3 class="in-block"><span id="The_.22PriceCostco.22_merger"></span><span class="mw-headline" id='The_"PriceCostco"_merger'>The "PriceCostco" merger</span><span class="mw-editsection"><a href="/w/index.php?title=Costco&amp;action=edit&amp;section=4" title='Edit section: The "PriceCostco" merger' data-section="4" class="mw-ui-icon mw-ui-icon-element mw-ui-icon-wikimedia-edit-base20 edit-page mw-ui-icon-flush-right">Edit</a></span></h3>
<p>In 1993, Costco and Price Club agreed to merge operations themselves after Price declined an offer from <a href="/wiki/Sam_Walton" title="Sam Walton">Sam Walton</a> and <a href="/wiki/Walmart" title="Walmart">Walmart</a> to merge Price Club with their warehouse store chain, <a href="/wiki/Sam%27s_Club" title="Sam's Club">Sam's Club</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-15" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-15">[15]</a></sup> Costco's business model and size were similar to those of Price Club, which made the merger more natural for both companies.<sup id="cite_ref-highlights_10-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-highlights-10">[10]</a></sup> The combined company took the name <b>PriceCostco</b>, and memberships became universal, meaning that a Price Club member could use their membership to shop at Costco and vice versa. PriceCostco boasted 206 locations generating $16<span class="nowrap"> </span>billion in annual sales.<sup id="cite_ref-membership_9-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-membership-9">[9]</a></sup> PriceCostco was initially led by executives from both companies, but in 1994, the Price brothers left the company to form <a href="/wiki/PriceSmart" title="PriceSmart">Price Enterprises</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-highlights_10-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-highlights-10">[10]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Costco-Nov-1994-SC-13E4_16-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Costco-Nov-1994-SC-13E4-16">[16]</a></sup> a warehouse club chain in Central America and the Caribbean unrelated to the current Costco.<sup id="cite_ref-17" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-17">[17]</a></sup></p><p>In 1997, Costco changed its name to Costco Wholesale Corporation, and all remaining Price Club locations were rebranded <span class="nowrap">as Costco.<sup id="cite_ref-membership_9-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-membership-9">[9]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-highlights_10-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-highlights-10">[10]</a></sup></span>
</p>
<h3 class="in-block"><span class="mw-headline" id="Locations">Locations</span><span class="mw-editsection"><a href="/w/index.php?title=Costco&amp;action=edit&amp;section=5" title="Edit section: Locations" data-section="5" class="mw-ui-icon mw-ui-icon-element mw-ui-icon-wikimedia-edit-base20 edit-page mw-ui-icon-flush-right">Edit</a></span></h3>

<p>On April 26, 2012, <a href="/wiki/CNBC" title="CNBC">CNBC</a> premiered its documentary, <i>The Costco Craze: Inside the Warehouse Giant</i>.<sup id="cite_ref-22" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-22">[22]</a></sup></p><p>In 2014, Costco was the third largest retailer in the United States.<sup id="cite_ref-23" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-23">[23]</a></sup> That year Costco announced plans to open an online store in China using <a href="/wiki/Alibaba_Group" title="Alibaba Group">Alibaba Group</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-24" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-24">[24]</a></sup></p>
<h3 class="in-block"><span class="mw-headline" id="Costco_today">Costco today</span><span class="mw-editsection"><a href="/w/index.php?title=Costco&amp;action=edit&amp;section=7" title="Edit section: Costco today" data-section="7" class="mw-ui-icon mw-ui-icon-element mw-ui-icon-wikimedia-edit-base20 edit-page mw-ui-icon-flush-right">Edit</a></span></h3>
<p>In the United States, Costco's main competitors operating membership warehouses are <a href="/wiki/Sam%27s_Club" title="Sam's Club">Sam's Club</a> and <a href="/wiki/BJ%27s_Wholesale_Club" title="BJ's Wholesale Club">BJ's Wholesale Club</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-25" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-25">[25]</a></sup> Costco employs 254,000 full and part-time <a href="/wiki/Employment" title="Employment">employees</a> worldwide.<sup id="cite_ref-2019_Annual_Report_1-21" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-2019_Annual_Report-1">[1]</a></sup> In 2016, Costco had 86.7<span class="nowrap"> </span>million members.<sup id="cite_ref-2018_Annual_Report_26-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-2018_Annual_Report-26">[26]</a></sup> In 2017, Costco had 90.3<span class="nowrap"> </span>million members.<sup id="cite_ref-Costco-IR-Profile_18-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Costco-IR-Profile-18">[18]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-2018_Annual_Report_26-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-2018_Annual_Report-26">[26]</a></sup> In 2018, Costco had 94.3<span class="nowrap"> </span>million members.<sup id="cite_ref-2018_Annual_Report_26-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-2018_Annual_Report-26">[26]</a></sup> In 2019, Costco had 98.5<span class="nowrap"> </span>million members.<sup id="cite_ref-2019_Annual_Report_1-22" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-2019_Annual_Report-1">[1]</a></sup></p><p>Costco was the first company to grow from zero to $3<span class="nowrap"> </span>billion in sales in under six years.<sup id="cite_ref-membership_9-5" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-membership-9">[9]</a></sup> For the fiscal year ending on August 31, 2012, the company's sales totaled $97.062<span class="nowrap"> </span>billion, with $1.709<span class="nowrap"> </span>billion net profit.<sup id="cite_ref-Costco-Oct-2012-10-K_27-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Costco-Oct-2012-10-K-27">[27]</a></sup> As of 2019<sup class="plainlinks noexcerpt noprint asof-tag update" style="display:none;"><a class="external text" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Costco&amp;action=edit">[update]</a></sup>, Costco is ranked <abbr title="Number">#</abbr>14 on the <a href="/wiki/Fortune_500" title="Fortune 500">Fortune 500</a> rankings of the largest United States corporations by total revenue.<sup id="cite_ref-Fortune_500_5-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Fortune_500-5">[5]</a></sup> The ACSI (The American Customer Satisfaction Index) named Costco number one in the specialty retail store industry with a score of 84 in 2014.<sup id="cite_ref-28" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-28">[28]</a></sup></p><p>From December 2013, Costco's board of directors was chaired by co-founder Jeffrey H. Brotman and included James Sinegal, co-founder and director, and two officers of the company: president/CEO <a href="/wiki/W._Craig_Jelinek" title="W. Craig Jelinek">W. Craig Jelinek</a> and CFO Richard A. Galanti. On August 1, 2017, Jeffrey Brotman died.<sup id="cite_ref-29" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-29">[29]</a></sup> As of August 2017<sup class="plainlinks noexcerpt noprint asof-tag update" style="display:none;"><a class="external text" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Costco&amp;action=edit">[update]</a></sup>, James Sinegal and W. Craig Jelinek remain on the board. Jim Sinegal stepped down in 2018.<sup id="cite_ref-2018_Annual_Report_26-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-2018_Annual_Report-26">[26]</a></sup></p>
</section><h2 class="section-heading" onclick="javascript:mfTempOpenSection(2)"><div class="mw-ui-icon mw-ui-icon-element indicator mw-ui-icon-small mw-ui-icon-flush-left"></div><span class="mw-headline" id="Finances">Finances</span><span class="mw-editsection"><a href="/w/index.php?title=Costco&amp;action=edit&amp;section=8" title="Edit section: Finances" data-section="8" class="mw-ui-icon mw-ui-icon-element mw-ui-icon-wikimedia-edit-base20 edit-page mw-ui-icon-flush-right">Edit</a></span></h2><section class="mf-section-2 collapsible-block" id="mf-section-2">
<p>For the fiscal year 2019, Costco reported earnings of US$3.659<span class="nowrap"> </span>billion, with an annual revenue of US$152.703<span class="nowrap"> </span>billion, an increase of 7.9% over the previous fiscal cycle. Costco's shares traded at over $205 per share, and its market capitalization was valued at over US$95.7<span class="nowrap"> </span>billion in October 2018.
</p>
