</td></tr></tbody></table></section><h2 class="section-heading" onclick="javascript:mfTempOpenSection(3)"><div class="mw-ui-icon mw-ui-icon-element indicator mw-ui-icon-small mw-ui-icon-flush-left"></div><span class="mw-headline" id="Sales_model">Sales model</span><span class="mw-editsection"><a href="/w/index.php?title=Costco&amp;action=edit&amp;section=9" title="Edit section: Sales model" data-section="9" class="mw-ui-icon mw-ui-icon-element mw-ui-icon-wikimedia-edit-base20 edit-page mw-ui-icon-flush-right">Edit</a></span></h2><section class="mf-section-3 collapsible-block" id="mf-section-3">
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:252px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Costcointerior.jpg" class="image"><noscript><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c5/Costcointerior.jpg/250px-Costcointerior.jpg" decoding="async" width="250" height="178" class="thumbimage" data-file-width="800" data-file-height="571"></noscript><span class="lazy-image-placeholder" style="width: 250px;height: 178px;" data-src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c5/Costcointerior.jpg/250px-Costcointerior.jpg" data-alt="" data-width="250" data-height="178" data-class="thumbimage"> </span></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Costcointerior.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Costco warehouse interior in <a href="/wiki/Mountain_View,_California" title="Mountain View, California">Mountain View, California</a></div></div></div>
<p>A typical Costco warehouse carries only 3,700 distinct products, while a typical Walmart Supercenter carries approximately 140,000 products.<sup id="cite_ref-Gabler_4-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Gabler-4">[4]</a></sup> If Costco feels the wholesale price of any individual product is too high, they will refuse to stock the product. For example, in November 2009, Costco announced that it would stop selling Coca-Cola products, because the soft-drink maker refused to lower its wholesale prices.<sup id="cite_ref-42" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-42">[42]</a></sup> Costco resumed selling Coca-Cola products the following month.<sup id="cite_ref-43" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-43">[43]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-44" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-44">[44]</a></sup></p><p>Lighting costs are reduced on sunny days, as most Costco locations have several skylights. During the day, electronic light meters measure how much light is coming in the skylights and turn off an appropriate percentage of the interior lights. During an average sunny day, it is normal for the center section of the warehouse not to have interior lights in use.<sup id="cite_ref-45" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-45">[45]</a></sup></p><p>Although the brand engages in visible efforts to reduce costs, the stores themselves are expensive.  In 2013, Costco spent approximately $80<span class="nowrap"> </span>million on each of the new stores it opened.<sup id="cite_ref-:1_46-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:1-46">[46]</a></sup>  The cost is partly driven by the cost of <a href="/wiki/Real_estate" title="Real estate">real estate</a>, as each new store means that they need enough space to support a building of approximately 150,000 square feet (14,000 m<sup>2</sup>) in size, a large parking lot, and often a gas station.<sup id="cite_ref-:1_46-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:1-46">[46]</a></sup></p><p>The company has no public relations department and does not buy outside advertising.<sup id="cite_ref-Gabler_4-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Gabler-4">[4]</a></sup></p><p>The company's rule is that no item may be marked up more than 14% over cost and no Kirkland Signature item may be marked up more than 15% over cost.<sup id="cite_ref-Gabler_4-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Gabler-4">[4]</a></sup> The company runs very lean, with overhead costs at about 10% of revenue and profit margins at 2%.<sup id="cite_ref-Gabler_4-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Gabler-4">[4]</a></sup> Costco's annual membership fees (US$60/year for Gold Star, US$120/year for Executive as of 2019<sup class="plainlinks noexcerpt noprint asof-tag update" style="display:none;"><a class="external text" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Costco&amp;action=edit">[update]</a></sup>)<sup id="cite_ref-Costco-Join_47-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Costco-Join-47">[47]</a></sup> account for 80 percent of Costco's <a href="/wiki/Gross_margin" title="Gross margin">gross margin</a> and 70 percent of its <a href="/wiki/Operating_income" class="mw-redirect" title="Operating income">operating income</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-48" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-48">[48]</a></sup></p>
</section><h2 class="section-heading" onclick="javascript:mfTempOpenSection(4)"><div class="mw-ui-icon mw-ui-icon-element indicator mw-ui-icon-small mw-ui-icon-flush-left"></div><span class="mw-headline" id="Products">Products</span><span class="mw-editsection"><a href="/w/index.php?title=Costco&amp;action=edit&amp;section=10" title="Edit section: Products" data-section="10" class="mw-ui-icon mw-ui-icon-element mw-ui-icon-wikimedia-edit-base20 edit-page mw-ui-icon-flush-right">Edit</a></span></h2><section class="mf-section-4 collapsible-block" id="mf-section-4">
<p>Costco has a frequently changing inventory and is known for carrying products for a time, then discontinuing them or using them as seasonal products.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (February 2014)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup> Over the years, Costco has gradually expanded its range of products and services. Initially, it preferred to sell only boxed products that could be dispensed by simply tearing the stretch wrap off a pallet.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (July 2019)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup> It now<sup class="noprint Inline-Template" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Manual_of_Style/Dates_and_numbers#Chronological_items" title="Wikipedia:Manual of Style/Dates and numbers"><span title="The time period mentioned near this tag is ambiguous. (July 2019)">when?</span></a></i>]</sup> sells many other products that are more difficult to handle, such as art, books, <a href="/wiki/Caskets" class="mw-redirect" title="Caskets">caskets</a>, clothing, computer software, fine wine, furniture, home appliances, home electronics, <a href="/wiki/Hot_tub" title="Hot tub">hot tubs</a>, jewelry, perishable items (such as dairy, fresh baked goods, flowers, fresh produce, meat, seafood), <a href="/wiki/Solar_panel" title="Solar panel">solar panels</a>, tires, and vacuum cleaners.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (July 2019)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup> Many warehouses also have <a href="/wiki/Filling_station" title="Filling station">gas stations</a>, <a href="/wiki/Pharmacy" title="Pharmacy">pharmacies</a>, <a href="/wiki/Hearing_aid" title="Hearing aid">hearing aid</a> centers, <a href="/wiki/Optometry" title="Optometry">optometrists</a>, eye and sunglass centers, <a href="/wiki/Photographic_processing" title="Photographic processing">photo processors</a>, and tire <a href="/wiki/Automobile_repair_shop" title="Automobile repair shop">garages</a>.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (July 2019)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup> The produce items that require refrigeration are kept in a walk-in refrigerator, and several locations even have a walk-in refrigerator for dairy items.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (July 2019)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup></p><p>Some locations have liquor stores, often kept separate from the main warehouse in order to comply with <a href="/wiki/Liquor_license" title="Liquor license">liquor license</a> restrictions. In some states (such as Texas), the liquor store must be owned and operated by a separate company with separate employees.<sup id="cite_ref-49" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-49">[49]</a></sup> In 2006, Costco lost a lawsuit against the state of Washington in which it was seeking to purchase wine directly from the producer, bypassing the <a href="/wiki/Alcoholic_beverage_control_state" title="Alcoholic beverage control state">state retail monopoly</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-50" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-50">[50]</a></sup> In Australia, Costco has to comply with regulations set by each state they choose to trade in;<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (July 2019)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup> their first store in the state of Victoria benefits from some of the most liberal alcohol licensing laws in that country, with retailers permitted to sell alcohol on shelves within the store, in a manner similar to most European countries.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (July 2019)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup> In the Canadian province of <a href="/wiki/Quebec" title="Quebec">Quebec</a>, beer and wine are sold within the stores from pallets.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (July 2019)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup></p>
<h3 class="in-block"><span class="mw-headline" id="Kirkland_Signature">Kirkland Signature</span><span class="mw-editsection"><a href="/w/index.php?title=Costco&amp;action=edit&amp;section=11" title="Edit section: Kirkland Signature" data-section="11" class="mw-ui-icon mw-ui-icon-element mw-ui-icon-wikimedia-edit-base20 edit-page mw-ui-icon-flush-right">Edit</a></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:180px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Kirkland_Signature_logo.svg" class="image"><noscript><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9f/Kirkland_Signature_logo.svg/178px-Kirkland_Signature_logo.svg.png" decoding="async" width="178" height="55" class="thumbimage" data-file-width="178" data-file-height="55"></noscript><span class="lazy-image-placeholder" style="width: 178px;height: 55px;" data-src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9f/Kirkland_Signature_logo.svg/178px-Kirkland_Signature_logo.svg.png" data-alt="" data-width="178" data-height="55" data-class="thumbimage"> </span></a>  <div class="thumbcaption">Kirkland Signature logo</div></div></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:152px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Kirkland_Signature_Drinking_Water_1.5L_20050508.jpg" class="image"><noscript><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/68/Kirkland_Signature_Drinking_Water_1.5L_20050508.jpg/150px-Kirkland_Signature_Drinking_Water_1.5L_20050508.jpg" decoding="async" width="150" height="200" class="thumbimage" data-file-width="960" data-file-height="1280"></noscript><span class="lazy-image-placeholder" style="width: 150px;height: 200px;" data-src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/68/Kirkland_Signature_Drinking_Water_1.5L_20050508.jpg/150px-Kirkland_Signature_Drinking_Water_1.5L_20050508.jpg" data-alt="" data-width="150" data-height="200" data-class="thumbimage"> </span></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Kirkland_Signature_Drinking_Water_1.5L_20050508.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Kirkland Signature branded <a href="/wiki/Bottled_water" title="Bottled water">bottled water</a>, pictured in 2005</div></div></div>
<p>"Kirkland Signature" is Costco's <a href="/wiki/Private_label" title="Private label">private label</a>. It is sold by Costco at their website and warehouses, and is trademarked by the company. Costco introduced Kirkland Signature as its private label in 1992, deriving the name from the location of Costco's then corporate headquarters, <a href="/wiki/Kirkland,_Washington" title="Kirkland, Washington">Kirkland, Washington</a> (their HQ later moved, roughly 12 miles (19 km), to <a href="/wiki/Issaquah,_Washington" title="Issaquah, Washington">Issaquah, Washington</a>).<sup id="cite_ref-51" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-51">[51]</a></sup> It accounts for almost a third of all Costco sales and is growing faster than Costco sales.<sup id="cite_ref-52" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-52">[52]</a></sup> Kirkland branded bottled water is produced by private label bottler <a href="/wiki/Niagara_Bottling" title="Niagara Bottling">Niagara Bottling</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-53" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-53">[53]</a></sup></p><p>The idea for the private label was to provide the appearance of brand name quality products at discounted prices.<sup id="cite_ref-54" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-54">[54]</a></sup> To counteract the consumer confidence problem common in store-name branding, Kirkland Signature occasionally employs <a href="/wiki/Co-branding" title="Co-branding">co-branding</a>. According to Costco, while consumers may be wary of same-store branding, they are less likely to be wary of brands that they are familiar with and trust.<sup id="cite_ref-55" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-55">[55]</a></sup></p>
</section><h2 class="section-heading" onclick="javascript:mfTempOpenSection(5)"><div class="mw-ui-icon mw-ui-icon-element indicator mw-ui-icon-small mw-ui-icon-flush-left"></div><span class="mw-headline" id="Publications">Publications</span><span class="mw-editsection"><a href="/w/index.php?title=Costco&amp;action=edit&amp;section=12" title="Edit section: Publications" data-section="12" class="mw-ui-icon mw-ui-icon-element mw-ui-icon-wikimedia-edit-base20 edit-page mw-ui-icon-flush-right">Edit</a></span></h2><section class="mf-section-5 collapsible-block" id="mf-section-5">
<p><i>The Costco Connection</i> is a magazine sent free to members of Costco; it can also be accessed online by anyone, free of charge.<sup id="cite_ref-56" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-56">[56]</a></sup> The magazine, established in 1987, features articles which regularly tie into the corporation along with business, celebrity features, cooking, entertaining, health, home improvement, and social articles, as well as coupons and ads. MediaPost reports: "While about 90% of the magazine's advertising is co-op, increasingly national advertisers such as Procter &amp; Gamble are buying space, notes Roeglin -- presumably because of the pub's gargantuan reach and the data it has on its subscribers (whose average household income is $156,000 a year). 'We see about 56% of our subscribers a month buy something at one of our stores based on something they've read in the magazine,' says Roeglin."<sup id="cite_ref-Robins,_J._Max_57-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Robins,_J._Max-57">[57]</a></sup> The magazine is the largest-circulation print monthly in the United States.<sup id="cite_ref-Robins,_J._Max_57-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Robins,_J._Max-57">[57]</a></sup> Costco also publishes the <i>Costco Household Almanac</i> and a cookbook series.<sup id="cite_ref-58" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-58">[58]</a></sup></p>
</section><h2 class="section-heading" onclick="javascript:mfTempOpenSection(6)"><div class="mw-ui-icon mw-ui-icon-element indicator mw-ui-icon-small mw-ui-icon-flush-left"></div><span class="mw-headline" id="Services">Services</span><span class="mw-editsection"><a href="/w/index.php?title=Costco&amp;action=edit&amp;section=13" title="Edit section: Services" data-section="13" class="mw-ui-icon mw-ui-icon-element mw-ui-icon-wikimedia-edit-base20 edit-page mw-ui-icon-flush-right">Edit</a></span></h2><section class="mf-section-6 collapsible-block" id="mf-section-6">
<h3 class="in-block"><span class="mw-headline" id="Concierge_service">Concierge service</span><span class="mw-editsection"><a href="/w/index.php?title=Costco&amp;action=edit&amp;section=14" title="Edit section: Concierge service" data-section="14" class="mw-ui-icon mw-ui-icon-element mw-ui-icon-wikimedia-edit-base20 edit-page mw-ui-icon-flush-right">Edit</a></span></h3>
<p>Costco offers a free "concierge" service to members who purchase electronics, to help answer questions regarding setup and use and avoid potential returns due to not understanding how to use the products.<sup id="cite_ref-costco.com_59-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-costco.com-59">[59]</a></sup></p><p>Costco acts as an investment broker and <a href="/wiki/Travel_agency" title="Travel agency">travel agent</a>. Costco has an agreement with <a href="/wiki/Ameriprise_Financial" title="Ameriprise Financial">Ameriprise</a> for auto and home insurance.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (July 2019)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup> In 2004, Costco offered an original artwork by artist <a href="/wiki/Pablo_Picasso" title="Pablo Picasso">Pablo Picasso</a> on their online store;<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (July 2019)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup> more recently<sup class="noprint Inline-Template" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Manual_of_Style/Dates_and_numbers#Chronological_items" title="Wikipedia:Manual of Style/Dates and numbers"><span title="The time period mentioned near this tag is ambiguous. (November 2009)">when?</span></a></i>]</sup> a highly regarded 1982 <a href="/wiki/Ch%C3%A2teau_Mouton_Rothschild" title="Château Mouton Rothschild">Mouton Rothschild</a> wine was offered as well as other rare wines in rotation.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (December 2008)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup></p><p>Costco Photo Center is a multi-functional photography printing lab offering services at the warehouses as well as through their web site, costcophotocenter.com. The website provides free unlimited digital file storage with a current membership. Previous to May or June 2010, Costco had an agreement with Mypublisher.com for custom book and calendar publishing.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (July 2019)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup> Now,<sup class="noprint Inline-Template" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Manual_of_Style/Dates_and_numbers#Chronological_items" title="Wikipedia:Manual of Style/Dates and numbers"><span title="The time period mentioned near this tag is ambiguous. (September 2012)">when?</span></a></i>]</sup> they print the photobooks and calendars themselves.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (July 2019)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup></p>
<h3 class="in-block"><span class="mw-headline" id="Costco_Auto_Program">Costco Auto Program</span><span class="mw-editsection"><a href="/w/index.php?title=Costco&amp;action=edit&amp;section=15" title="Edit section: Costco Auto Program" data-section="15" class="mw-ui-icon mw-ui-icon-element mw-ui-icon-wikimedia-edit-base20 edit-page mw-ui-icon-flush-right">Edit</a></span></h3>
<p>As of September 2015<sup class="plainlinks noexcerpt noprint asof-tag update" style="display:none;"><a class="external text" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Costco&amp;action=edit">[update]</a></sup>, Costco was the second largest auto seller in the US, just behind AutoNation.<sup id="cite_ref-Addicted_to_Costo_60-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Addicted_to_Costo-60">[60]</a></sup> Costco regularly teams up with various automobile manufacturers to offer special deals to customers, e.g., Polaris (a leading seller of powersport vehicles) in 4Q2015<sup id="cite_ref-Addicted_to_Costo_60-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Addicted_to_Costo-60">[60]</a></sup> and <a href="/wiki/General_Motors" title="General Motors">General Motors</a> from October 2015 through January 2016.<sup id="cite_ref-addictedtocostco.com_61-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-addictedtocostco.com-61">[61]</a></sup> <i>Addicted to Costco</i> lists the following as some benefits of the Costco Auto Program:<sup id="cite_ref-addictedtocostco.com_61-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-addictedtocostco.com-61">[61]</a></sup></p>
<ul><li>A low, prearranged price for Costco members</li>
<li>All available national manufacturer incentives</li>
<li>More than 3,000 dealerships nationwide, with specially trained employees to assist Costco members</li></ul><h3 class="in-block"><span class="mw-headline" id="Costco_business_services">Costco business services</span><span class="mw-editsection"><a href="/w/index.php?title=Costco&amp;action=edit&amp;section=16" title="Edit section: Costco business services" data-section="16" class="mw-ui-icon mw-ui-icon-element mw-ui-icon-wikimedia-edit-base20 edit-page mw-ui-icon-flush-right">Edit</a></span></h3>
<p>On March 9, 2005, NOVA Information Systems (NOVA) partnered with Costco to market and support <a href="/wiki/Payment_processing" class="mw-redirect" title="Payment processing">payment processing</a> services to Costco Canada's Business Executive Members.<sup id="cite_ref-62" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-62">[62]</a></sup></p>
<h3 class="in-block"><span class="mw-headline" id="Costco_Optical">Costco Optical</span><span class="mw-editsection"><a href="/w/index.php?title=Costco&amp;action=edit&amp;section=17" title="Edit section: Costco Optical" data-section="17" class="mw-ui-icon mw-ui-icon-element mw-ui-icon-wikimedia-edit-base20 edit-page mw-ui-icon-flush-right">Edit</a></span></h3>
<p>Costco Optical ranks as the fifth-largest optical company in the US, as of 2015<sup class="plainlinks noexcerpt noprint asof-tag update" style="display:none;"><a class="external text" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Costco&amp;action=edit">[update]</a></sup>.<sup id="cite_ref-63" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-63">[63]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Optometry" title="Optometry">Optometrists</a> working at Costco locations will see patients without Costco memberships,<sup id="cite_ref-64" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-64">[64]</a></sup> although a membership is required to fill a prescription at the optical department.<sup id="cite_ref-65" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-65">[65]</a></sup></p>
<h3 class="in-block"><span class="mw-headline" id="Costco_Travel">Costco Travel</span><span class="mw-editsection"><a href="/w/index.php?title=Costco&amp;action=edit&amp;section=18" title="Edit section: Costco Travel" data-section="18" class="mw-ui-icon mw-ui-icon-element mw-ui-icon-wikimedia-edit-base20 edit-page mw-ui-icon-flush-right">Edit</a></span></h3>
<p>Costco Travel is a wholly owned subsidiary of Costco Wholesale and offers leisure travel to Costco members of the United States and Canada.<sup id="cite_ref-66" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-66">[66]</a></sup> The program was established in 2000 as a service to Costco members. Costco Travel's offices are located in <a href="/wiki/Issaquah,_Washington" title="Issaquah, Washington">Issaquah, Washington</a>, adjacent to Costco's corporate headquarters. Costco Travel employs over 700 travel professionals, all of them Costco employees.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (July 2019)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup></p><p>The program offers vacation packages to the Caribbean, Europe, Florida, Hawaii, Las Vegas, Mexico, and the South Pacific.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (September 2012)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup> Other products include car rentals, cruises, guided vacations, and theme park packages. Select products feature additional benefits for Costco Executive Members.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (September 2012)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup></p><p>The program is marketed directly to Costco members through various Costco avenues, including the <i>Travel Guide to Savings</i> (found in all U.S. Costco warehouses) and in the Travel section of Costco.com.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (September 2012)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup></p>
<h3 class="in-block"><span class="mw-headline" id="Food_service">Food service</span><span class="mw-editsection"><a href="/w/index.php?title=Costco&amp;action=edit&amp;section=19" title="Edit section: Food service" data-section="19" class="mw-ui-icon mw-ui-icon-element mw-ui-icon-wikimedia-edit-base20 edit-page mw-ui-icon-flush-right">Edit</a></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Costco-foodcourt.jpg" class="image"><noscript><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/51/Costco-foodcourt.jpg/220px-Costco-foodcourt.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="157" class="thumbimage" data-file-width="700" data-file-height="500"></noscript><span class="lazy-image-placeholder" style="width: 220px;height: 157px;" data-src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/51/Costco-foodcourt.jpg/220px-Costco-foodcourt.jpg" data-alt="" data-width="220" data-height="157" data-class="thumbimage"> </span></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Costco-foodcourt.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Concession_stand" title="Concession stand">Food concession stand</a> at the Costco warehouse in <a href="/wiki/Overland_Park,_Kansas" title="Overland Park, Kansas">Overland Park, Kansas</a></div></div></div>
<p>Most (if not all) Costco locations have a <a href="/wiki/Food_court" title="Food court">food court</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-67" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-67">[67]</a></sup> They can be indoors or outdoors,<sup id="cite_ref-68" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-68">[68]</a></sup> but the menu is essentially the same: hot dog with drink (one of the food court's most popular items), pizza, frozen yogurt, various drinks, baked items, and sandwiches.<sup id="cite_ref-69" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-69">[69]</a></sup> Sometimes, items are added to the menu seasonally. Costco offers a quarter-pound 100% beef <a href="/wiki/Hot_dog" title="Hot dog">hot dog</a> and 20 US fluid ounces (590 ml) drink (with refills) for <span style="white-space: nowrap">US$1.50</span>, the same price since 1985.<sup id="cite_ref-70" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-70">[70]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-71" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-71">[71]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-No_Polish_Dog_72-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-No_Polish_Dog-72">[72]</a></sup> In Australia, the hot dog is made of pork and is sold with a large soda for <a href="/wiki/Australian_dollar" title="Australian dollar">AUD$</a>1.99. In Canada, the price for a hot dog and soda with refills is <a href="/wiki/Canadian_dollar" title="Canadian dollar">C$</a>1.50.<sup id="cite_ref-Food_court_73-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Food_court-73">[73]</a></sup> In Mexico, the hot dog is made of 100% beef and includes a drink (with refills) for <a href="/wiki/Mexican_peso" title="Mexican peso">MXN$</a>35. In the UK, the hot dog is also made from beef and customers also get a drink (with refills) for <a href="/wiki/Pound_sterling" title="Pound sterling">£</a>1.50. Costco sold more than 137<span class="nowrap"> </span>million quarter-pound (113 g) hot dogs in its food courts in 2017.<sup id="cite_ref-No_Polish_Dog_72-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-No_Polish_Dog-72">[72]</a></sup></p><p>In Taiwan and Japan, the hot dog is made of pork as well.<sup id="cite_ref-74" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-74">[74]</a></sup></p><p>Cheese, pepperoni, veggie, or combo pizza is also available in most locations, and can usually be ordered to go, making Costco arguably the 14th largest pizza chain in the U.S. in 2010.<sup id="cite_ref-75" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-75">[75]</a></sup> Frozen yogurt is also served in chocolate, vanilla, or swirl. Costco also offers fruit <a href="/wiki/Smoothie" title="Smoothie">smoothies</a>, <a href="/wiki/Latte" title="Latte">latte</a> freeze (without chocolate), mocha freeze (with chocolate), beef bake,<sup id="cite_ref-76" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-76">[76]</a></sup> chicken bake, turkey <a href="/wiki/Provolone" title="Provolone">provolone</a> sandwiches, twisted <a href="/wiki/Churro" title="Churro">churros</a>, chicken <a href="/wiki/Caesar_salad" title="Caesar salad">Caesar salads</a>, beef brisket sandwiches, organic beef-based cheeseburgers, beef chili with beans, and in some locations, <a href="/wiki/Gelato" title="Gelato">gelato</a>. Various locations also began offering acai bowls in 2018. <a href="/wiki/French_fries" title="French fries">French fries</a> are also offered in some locations. Some of the food court items are only available in certain countries. For example, the <a href="/wiki/Bulgogi" title="Bulgogi">bulgogi</a> bake is only available in Taiwan, Korea, and Japan; <a href="/wiki/Poutine" title="Poutine">poutine</a> is only available in Canada; and plokkari only in Iceland. There are, however, temporary menu items available exclusively in several countries, like the <i>pizza al pastor</i> in Mexico.<sup id="cite_ref-77" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-77">[77]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-78" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-78">[78]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-79" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-79">[79]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-80" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-80">[80]</a></sup> The nutrition data for the Costco Food Court items is posted online.
</p><p>Due to slow sales, in 2009, the <a href="/wiki/Pretzel" title="Pretzel">pretzel</a> was replaced by the churro.<sup id="cite_ref-81" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-81">[81]</a></sup> In April 2013, <a href="/wiki/Pepsi" title="Pepsi">Pepsi</a> replaced all <a href="/wiki/Coca-Cola" title="Coca-Cola">Coca-Cola</a> fountain drinks at U.S. locations because Coke had raised its prices; this helped keep the hot dog combo with soda at its original <span style="white-space: nowrap">US$1.50</span> price.<sup id="cite_ref-82" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-82">[82]</a></sup></p><p>In select Costco food courts, Costco is selling cheeseburgers for a limited time to experiment sales. It will possibly be a new menu item if it has a success.<sup id="cite_ref-83" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-83">[83]</a></sup><sup class="noprint Inline-Template" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Manual_of_Style/Dates_and_numbers#Chronological_items" title="Wikipedia:Manual of Style/Dates and numbers"><span title="The date of the event predicted near this tag has passed. (December 2019)">needs update</span></a></i>]</sup></p>
<h3 class="in-block"><span class="mw-headline" id="Online_photo_site">Online photo site</span><span class="mw-editsection"><a href="/w/index.php?title=Costco&amp;action=edit&amp;section=20" title="Edit section: Online photo site" data-section="20" class="mw-ui-icon mw-ui-icon-element mw-ui-icon-wikimedia-edit-base20 edit-page mw-ui-icon-flush-right">Edit</a></span></h3>
<p>In December 2005, Costco signed an agreement with PhotoChannel Networks Inc., whereby Costco could deploy the PNI Digital Media Platform to offer online photo printing for Costco members through the website.<sup id="cite_ref-84" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-84">[84]</a></sup></p><p>On July 17, 2015, Costco disabled their online photo site.<sup id="cite_ref-85" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-85">[85]</a></sup> In common with other retailers,<sup id="cite_ref-86" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-86">[86]</a></sup> there is currently<sup class="noprint Inline-Template" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Manual_of_Style/Dates_and_numbers#Chronological_items" title="Wikipedia:Manual of Style/Dates and numbers"><span title="The time period mentioned near this tag is ambiguous. (August 2019)">when?</span></a></i>]</sup> no confirmation about whether hackers had stolen Costco customers' photographs or data. As of August 1, 2015<sup class="plainlinks noexcerpt noprint asof-tag update" style="display:none;"><a class="external text" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Costco&amp;action=edit">[update]</a></sup>, Costco was estimating the website might return in mid-August, after a four-week outage.<sup id="cite_ref-87" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-87">[87]</a></sup></p>
<h3 class="in-block"><span class="mw-headline" id="Online_shopping">Online shopping</span><span class="mw-editsection"><a href="/w/index.php?title=Costco&amp;action=edit&amp;section=21" title="Edit section: Online shopping" data-section="21" class="mw-ui-icon mw-ui-icon-element mw-ui-icon-wikimedia-edit-base20 edit-page mw-ui-icon-flush-right">Edit</a></span></h3>
<p>On April 17, 2001, Costco Wholesale opened a B2B (Business to Business) online shopping site at <i>Costco.com</i> for faster and easier business shopping.<sup id="cite_ref-88" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-88">[88]</a></sup></p><p>The domain <i>Costco.com</i> attracted at least 58<span class="nowrap"> </span>million visitors in 2008, according to a <a href="/wiki/Compete.com" title="Compete.com">Compete.com</a> survey.<sup id="cite_ref-89" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-89">[89]</a></sup> Costco.com is for United States members; costco.ca is for Canadian members, and other countries, such as Mexico, South Korea, Taiwan and the UK, each has its own online Costco shopping website.
</p><p><a href="/wiki/Instacart" title="Instacart">Instacart</a> offers Costco delivery in a select number of states including Arizona, California, Colorado, Florida, Georgia, Illinois, Indiana, Massachusetts, Maryland, Minnesota, Missouri, North Carolina, New Jersey, New York, Oregon, Tennessee, Texas, Virginia, Washington, and the District of Columbia.<sup id="cite_ref-90" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-90">[90]</a></sup> No membership is needed to order from Costco on Instacart, but Instacart charges delivery fees and the prices may not necessarily be the same as in a Costco warehouse. Similarly, in March 2017, Costco initiated a partnership with <a href="/wiki/Shipt" title="Shipt">Shipt</a>, an online grocery delivery service. Unlike Instacart, Shipt charges its own membership fee, $99 a year or $14 a month, in exchange for free delivery on orders over $35. As of November 2018<sup class="plainlinks noexcerpt noprint asof-tag update" style="display:none;"><a class="external text" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Costco&amp;action=edit">[update]</a></sup>, Shipt offers Costco delivery in select Florida markets.<sup id="cite_ref-91" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-91">[91]</a></sup></p><p>In October 2017, Costco launched same-day and two-day grocery delivery options for members.<sup id="cite_ref-92" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-92">[92]</a></sup>Costco Business Centers provide a variety of different goods for clients that differ greatly from their traditional in-store wares. More than 70% of the items that can be acquired from a Costco Business Center cannot be found in a typical Costco store. They are primarily utilized by smaller businesses who seek to make purchases in bulk. There is a delivery charge of $25 for orders that are below $250.<sup id="cite_ref-93" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-93">[93]</a></sup></p>
<h3 class="in-block"><span class="mw-headline" id="Costco_credit_card">Costco credit card</span><span class="mw-editsection"><a href="/w/index.php?title=Costco&amp;action=edit&amp;section=22" title="Edit section: Costco credit card" data-section="22" class="mw-ui-icon mw-ui-icon-element mw-ui-icon-wikimedia-edit-base20 edit-page mw-ui-icon-flush-right">Edit</a></span></h3>
<p>On April 1, 2016, <a href="/wiki/Citigroup" title="Citigroup">Citigroup</a> became the exclusive issuer of Costco's branded credit cards.<sup id="cite_ref-94" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-94">[94]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-95" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-95">[95]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-96" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-96">[96]</a></sup></p>
</section><h2 class="section-heading" onclick="javascript:mfTempOpenSection(7)"><div class="mw-ui-icon mw-ui-icon-element indicator mw-ui-icon-small mw-ui-icon-flush-left"></div><span class="mw-headline" id="Labor_relations">Labor relations</span><span class="mw-editsection"><a href="/w/index.php?title=Costco&amp;action=edit&amp;section=23" title="Edit section: Labor relations" data-section="23" class="mw-ui-icon mw-ui-icon-element mw-ui-icon-wikimedia-edit-base20 edit-page mw-ui-icon-flush-right">Edit</a></span></h2><section class="mf-section-7 collapsible-block" id="mf-section-7">
<h3 class="in-block"><span class="mw-headline" id="Employee_Rights">Employee Rights</span><span class="mw-editsection"><a href="/w/index.php?title=Costco&amp;action=edit&amp;section=24" title="Edit section: Employee Rights" data-section="24" class="mw-ui-icon mw-ui-icon-element mw-ui-icon-wikimedia-edit-base20 edit-page mw-ui-icon-flush-right">Edit</a></span></h3>
<p>While some former Price Club locations in California and the northeastern United States are staffed by <a href="/wiki/Teamsters" class="mw-redirect" title="Teamsters">Teamsters</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-97" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-97">[97]</a></sup> the majority of Costco locations are not unionized although there seemed to be a move in 2012 to unionize some locations in Canada.<sup id="cite_ref-98" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-98">[98]</a></sup> The non-union locations have revisions to their Costco Employee Agreement every three years concurrent with union contract ratifications in locations with collective bargaining agreements. The Employee Agreement sets forth such things as benefits, compensations, wages, disciplinary procedures, paid holidays, bonuses, and seniority. The Employee Agreement is subject to change by Costco at any time and offers no absolute protection to the workers. As of March 2011<sup class="plainlinks noexcerpt noprint asof-tag update" style="display:none;"><a class="external text" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Costco&amp;action=edit">[update]</a></sup>, non-supervisory hourly wages ranged from $11.00 to $21.00 in the U.S., $11.00 to $22.15 in Canada, and £8.50 to £11.50 in the United Kingdom. In the U.S. as of 2005<sup class="plainlinks noexcerpt noprint asof-tag update" style="display:none;"><a class="external text" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Costco&amp;action=edit">[update]</a></sup>, eighty-five<span class="nowrap"> </span>percent of Costco's workers had <a href="/wiki/Health_insurance" title="Health insurance">health insurance</a>, compared with less than fifty percent at Walmart and Target.<sup id="cite_ref-99" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-99">[99]</a></sup> Health benefits include coverage through <a href="/wiki/Aetna" title="Aetna">Aetna</a>, remote primary care through <a href="/wiki/Teladoc" class="mw-redirect" title="Teladoc">Teladoc</a>, second opinions and clinical navigation by <a href="/wiki/Grand_Rounds,_Inc." title="Grand Rounds, Inc.">Grand Rounds</a>, and wellness coaching by Omada.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (July 2019)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup></p>
<h3 class="in-block"><span class="mw-headline" id="Contractors">Contractors</span><span class="mw-editsection"><a href="/w/index.php?title=Costco&amp;action=edit&amp;section=25" title="Edit section: Contractors" data-section="25" class="mw-ui-icon mw-ui-icon-element mw-ui-icon-wikimedia-edit-base20 edit-page mw-ui-icon-flush-right">Edit</a></span></h3>
<p>Product-demonstration (e.g., food samples) employees work for an independent company. In the western U.S., the company is called Warehouse Demo Services, Kirkland, Washington.<sup id="cite_ref-100" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-100">[100]</a></sup> Costco also uses Club Demonstration Services (CDS), based in San Diego, California.<sup id="cite_ref-101" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-101">[101]</a></sup> Demonstration employees receive a pay and benefit package that is less than that of Costco employees. As of August 1, 2017<sup class="plainlinks noexcerpt noprint asof-tag update" style="display:none;"><a class="external text" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Costco&amp;action=edit">[update]</a></sup>, demonstrations/samples are provided by CDS in Canada.<sup id="cite_ref-We_Are_Family_102-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-We_Are_Family-102">[102]</a></sup></p>
<h3 class="in-block"><span class="mw-headline" id="Public_Health">Public Health</span><span class="mw-editsection"><a href="/w/index.php?title=Costco&amp;action=edit&amp;section=26" title="Edit section: Public Health" data-section="26" class="mw-ui-icon mw-ui-icon-element mw-ui-icon-wikimedia-edit-base20 edit-page mw-ui-icon-flush-right">Edit</a></span></h3>
<p>Following the <a href="/wiki/Coronavirus_disease_2019" title="Coronavirus disease 2019">COVID-19</a> outbreak, the first Costco store in Perth, Australia unexpectedly opened on March 19, 2020 without an opening ceremony and earlier than its planned time of 8:00AM due to high demand, especially for toilet paper products, to ease panic buying in mainstream supermarkets in Australia, although toliet paper was limited to only 1 per transaction. Carts and other objects were cleaned regularly to minimize the risk of contracting the virus.
</p><p>As of March 6, 2020, Costco contractor CDS has temporarily stopped providing free food samples in several Costco stores globally amid public health concerns regarding <a href="/wiki/Coronavirus_disease_2019" title="Coronavirus disease 2019">COVID-19</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-103" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-103">[103]</a></sup></p>
</section><h2 class="section-heading" onclick="javascript:mfTempOpenSection(8)"><div class="mw-ui-icon mw-ui-icon-element indicator mw-ui-icon-small mw-ui-icon-flush-left"></div><span class="mw-headline" id="International_locations_and_other_centers">International locations and other centers</span><span class="mw-editsection"><a href="/w/index.php?title=Costco&amp;action=edit&amp;section=27" title="Edit section: International locations and other centers" data-section="27" class="mw-ui-icon mw-ui-icon-element mw-ui-icon-wikimedia-edit-base20 edit-page mw-ui-icon-flush-right">Edit</a></span></h2><section class="mf-section-8 collapsible-block" id="mf-section-8">
<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Costco_Perth-Front_Enterance_(During_First_Morning).jpg" class="image"><noscript><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/dd/Costco_Perth-Front_Enterance_%28During_First_Morning%29.jpg/220px-Costco_Perth-Front_Enterance_%28During_First_Morning%29.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="124" class="thumbimage" data-file-width="3264" data-file-height="1836"></noscript><span class="lazy-image-placeholder" style="width: 220px;height: 124px;" data-src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/dd/Costco_Perth-Front_Enterance_%28During_First_Morning%29.jpg/220px-Costco_Perth-Front_Enterance_%28During_First_Morning%29.jpg" data-alt="" data-width="220" data-height="124" data-class="thumbimage"> </span></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Costco_Perth-Front_Enterance_(During_First_Morning).jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Costco at Perth Airport, opened on 19th March 2020.</div></div></div>
<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Aerial_perspective_of_the_Costco_roof_at_the_Docklands._March_2019.jpg" class="image"><noscript><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c4/Aerial_perspective_of_the_Costco_roof_at_the_Docklands._March_2019.jpg/220px-Aerial_perspective_of_the_Costco_roof_at_the_Docklands._March_2019.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="124" class="thumbimage" data-file-width="4000" data-file-height="2250"></noscript><span class="lazy-image-placeholder" style="width: 220px;height: 124px;" data-src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c4/Aerial_perspective_of_the_Costco_roof_at_the_Docklands._March_2019.jpg/220px-Aerial_perspective_of_the_Costco_roof_at_the_Docklands._March_2019.jpg" data-alt="" data-width="220" data-height="124" data-class="thumbimage"> </span></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Aerial_perspective_of_the_Costco_roof_at_the_Docklands._March_2019.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Aerial perspective of the Costco roof at Melbourne's Docklands store. March 2019.</div></div></div>
<p>Warehouses outside the U.S. are similar to those in the US. Layout, signage, and even parking lot markings are generally identical to warehouses in the US.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (October 2009)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup> Food court menus are tailored to international tastes, with <a href="/wiki/Australian_and_New_Zealand_meat_pie" class="mw-redirect" title="Australian and New Zealand meat pie">meat pies</a> on offer in Australia, <a href="/wiki/Poutine" title="Poutine">poutine</a> in Canada, seafood-topped pizza in Asian locations, <a href="/wiki/Tacos_al_pastor" class="mw-redirect" title="Tacos al pastor">pastor taco</a>-topped pizzas in Mexico, <a href="/wiki/Clam_chowder" title="Clam chowder">clam chowder</a> in Japan, South Korea, and Taiwan, <a href="/w/index.php?title=Plokkfiskur&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Plokkfiskur (page does not exist)">plokkfiskur</a> in Iceland and <a href="/wiki/Jacket_potatoes" class="mw-redirect" title="Jacket potatoes">jacket potatoes</a> in the UK.<sup id="cite_ref-buckscoopcostcomelbourne_104-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-buckscoopcostcomelbourne-104">[104]</a></sup> Additionally, Costco has led a strategic initiative within the past year to enhance their merchandise mix available within international warehouses to tailor products to local tastes, with a mix of both American and local products available.
</p>
<h3 class="in-block"><span class="mw-headline" id="Expansion_worldwide">Expansion worldwide</span><span class="mw-editsection"><a href="/w/index.php?title=Costco&amp;action=edit&amp;section=28" title="Edit section: Expansion worldwide" data-section="28" class="mw-ui-icon mw-ui-icon-element mw-ui-icon-wikimedia-edit-base20 edit-page mw-ui-icon-flush-right">Edit</a></span></h3>
<p>Costco announced it opened 29 new locations in 2016, the most in one year since 2007.<sup id="cite_ref-105" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-105">[105]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-highlights_2017_106-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-highlights_2017-106">[106]</a></sup> Span Construction, led by <a href="/wiki/King_Husein" title="King Husein">King Husein</a>, has been constructing almost all of Costco's buildings since 1989.<sup id="cite_ref-metal_107-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-metal-107">[107]</a></sup></p><p>In August 2019, Costco opened its first Chinese location in Shanghai. The popularity of the store's opening led to its opening day being cut short over safety concerns.<sup id="cite_ref-108" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-108">[108]</a></sup></p>
<h3 class="in-block"><span class="mw-headline" id="Largest_location">Largest location</span><span class="mw-editsection"><a href="/w/index.php?title=Costco&amp;action=edit&amp;section=29" title="Edit section: Largest location" data-section="29" class="mw-ui-icon mw-ui-icon-element mw-ui-icon-wikimedia-edit-base20 edit-page mw-ui-icon-flush-right">Edit</a></span></h3>
<p>In 2005, the world's largest Costco was located in <a href="/wiki/Hillsboro,_Oregon" title="Hillsboro, Oregon">Hillsboro, Oregon</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-109" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-109">[109]</a></sup> In 2015, Costco completed an expansion in <a href="/wiki/Salt_Lake_City" title="Salt Lake City">Salt Lake City</a>, making it the new largest Costco at 235,000 sq ft (21,800 m<sup>2</sup>).<sup id="cite_ref-110" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-110">[110]</a></sup> In 2011, Costco's highest volume store was in Seoul, South Korea.<sup id="cite_ref-111" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-111">[111]</a></sup> Taiwan's Taichung ranks at the very top in the number of members and is second in the world in sales volume (the exact figures are confidential), behind South Korea's Yangjae store in Seoul; moreover, 13 Costco operations in Taiwan, three – Taichung, Neihu, and Chungho – rank in the top 10 in the world in sales volume.<sup id="cite_ref-112" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-112">[112]</a></sup></p>
<h3 class="in-block"><span class="mw-headline" id="Costco_Business_Centers">Costco Business Centers</span><span class="mw-editsection"><a href="/w/index.php?title=Costco&amp;action=edit&amp;section=30" title="Edit section: Costco Business Centers" data-section="30" class="mw-ui-icon mw-ui-icon-element mw-ui-icon-wikimedia-edit-base20 edit-page mw-ui-icon-flush-right">Edit</a></span></h3>
<p>Costco Business Centers are warehouses similar to regular Costco warehouses, and are open to all Costco members, regardless of membership type. Their merchandise, though, cater predominantly to <a href="/wiki/Business" title="Business">enterprises</a>, with a focus on <a href="/wiki/Small_business" title="Small business">small businesses</a>. Business Centers do not carry most consumer items like clothing, jewelry, media, and tires, while carrying larger quantities and more options for the business products they do carry.<sup id="cite_ref-lvsun_113-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-lvsun-113">[113]</a></sup> They do not offer most of the consumer-oriented services found at regular Costco warehouses, but some locations do have a food court or a gas station or both. Also unlike regular warehouses, most Costco Business Centers have a Print &amp; Copy Center which provides <a href="/wiki/Printing_shop" class="mw-redirect" title="Printing shop">printing professional services</a>. They have large <a href="/wiki/Parking_space" title="Parking space">parking spaces</a> for trucks and are capable of <a href="/wiki/Home_delivery" class="mw-redirect" title="Home delivery">delivering goods to businesses</a> in bulk quantities. Finally, opening hours are shorter than regular warehouses (usually opening at 7:00 am on Mondays to Saturdays and closed on Sundays), while discounts and coupons for Business Centers are issued separately from regular warehouses.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (March 2017)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup></p>
<h4 class="in-block"><span class="mw-headline" id="Locations_2">Locations</span><span class="mw-editsection"><a href="/w/index.php?title=Costco&amp;action=edit&amp;section=31" title="Edit section: Locations" data-section="31" class="mw-ui-icon mw-ui-icon-element mw-ui-icon-wikimedia-edit-base20 edit-page mw-ui-icon-flush-right">Edit</a></span></h4>
<p>As of August 2017<sup class="plainlinks noexcerpt noprint asof-tag update" style="display:none;"><a class="external text" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Costco&amp;action=edit">[update]</a></sup>, there are 17 Costco Business Centers in the United States, located in <a href="/wiki/Orlando,_Florida" title="Orlando, Florida">Orlando, Florida</a>; <a href="/wiki/Phoenix,_Arizona" title="Phoenix, Arizona">Phoenix, Arizona</a>; California (<a href="/wiki/Commerce,_California" title="Commerce, California">Commerce</a>, <a href="/wiki/Hawthorne,_California" title="Hawthorne, California">Hawthorne</a>, <a href="/wiki/Hayward,_California" title="Hayward, California">Hayward</a>, <a href="/wiki/North_Hollywood,_Los_Angeles" title="North Hollywood, Los Angeles">North Hollywood</a>, <a href="/wiki/San_Diego" title="San Diego">San Diego</a>, <a href="/wiki/South_San_Francisco,_California" title="South San Francisco, California">South San Francisco</a> and <a href="/wiki/Westminster,_California" title="Westminster, California">Westminster</a>); <a href="/wiki/Denver" title="Denver">Denver, Colorado</a>; <a href="/wiki/Morrow,_Georgia" title="Morrow, Georgia">Morrow, Georgia</a>; <a href="/wiki/Bedford_Park,_Illinois" title="Bedford Park, Illinois">Bedford Park, Illinois</a>; <a href="/wiki/Hackensack,_New_Jersey" title="Hackensack, New Jersey">Hackensack, New Jersey</a>; <a href="/wiki/Las_Vegas" title="Las Vegas">Las Vegas, Nevada</a>; and Washington (<a href="/wiki/Lynnwood,_Washington" title="Lynnwood, Washington">Lynnwood</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Fife,_Washington" title="Fife, Washington">Fife</a>).<sup id="cite_ref-sddt10_114-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-sddt10-114">[114]</a></sup></p><p>The first Costco Business Center outside the U.S. opened in Canada in <a href="/wiki/Scarborough,_Toronto" title="Scarborough, Toronto">Scarborough, Toronto</a> in spring 2017.<sup id="cite_ref-BusinessCentreCA_115-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-BusinessCentreCA-115">[115]</a></sup></p>
<h3 class="in-block"><span class="mw-headline" id="Vertical_Integration">Vertical Integration</span><span class="mw-editsection"><a href="/w/index.php?title=Costco&amp;action=edit&amp;section=32" title="Edit section: Vertical Integration" data-section="32" class="mw-ui-icon mw-ui-icon-element mw-ui-icon-wikimedia-edit-base20 edit-page mw-ui-icon-flush-right">Edit</a></span></h3>
<p>Like many other retailers <a href="/wiki/Vertical_integration" title="Vertical integration">vertically integrating</a> their food supply chains, Costco has brought in-house poultry production for their <a href="/wiki/Rotisserie_chicken" title="Rotisserie chicken">rotisserie chickens</a>, which are a major driver of customer traffic and sales.<sup id="cite_ref-116" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-116">[116]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-117" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-117">[117]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-CNN_chicken_118-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-CNN_chicken-118">[118]</a></sup> This is to allow keeping their pricing intact while maintaining a consistent quality control of its chickens as a result of annual growth of per-capita <a href="/wiki/Chicken" title="Chicken">chicken</a> consumption in the United States.<sup id="cite_ref-119" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-119">[119]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-CNN_chicken_118-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-CNN_chicken-118">[118]</a></sup></p>
</section><h2 class="section-heading" onclick="javascript:mfTempOpenSection(9)"><div class="mw-ui-icon mw-ui-icon-element indicator mw-ui-icon-small mw-ui-icon-flush-left"></div><span class="mw-headline" id="Discontinued_concepts">Discontinued concepts</span><span class="mw-editsection"><a href="/w/index.php?title=Costco&amp;action=edit&amp;section=33" title="Edit section: Discontinued concepts" data-section="33" class="mw-ui-icon mw-ui-icon-element mw-ui-icon-wikimedia-edit-base20 edit-page mw-ui-icon-flush-right">Edit</a></span></h2><section class="mf-section-9 collapsible-block" id="mf-section-9">
<h3 class="in-block"><span class="mw-headline" id="Costco_Home">Costco Home</span><span class="mw-editsection"><a href="/w/index.php?title=Costco&amp;action=edit&amp;section=34" title="Edit section: Costco Home" data-section="34" class="mw-ui-icon mw-ui-icon-element mw-ui-icon-wikimedia-edit-base20 edit-page mw-ui-icon-flush-right">Edit</a></span></h3>
<p>The first Costco Home warehouse opened in 1983, and was rebuilt / expanded in 2002, in Seattle.<sup id="cite_ref-120" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-120">[120]</a></sup> The warehouse's concept was to combine the value, setting and members-only elements of Costco's warehouse clubs with the product array one would find at an upscale home store, such as <a href="/wiki/Fortunoff" title="Fortunoff">Fortunoff</a> or <a href="/wiki/Crate_%26_Barrel" title="Crate &amp; Barrel">Crate &amp; Barrel</a>. The Costco Home warehouses sold furniture, housewares, kitchen products and accessories from higher-end brands such as Lexington, <a href="/wiki/Polo_Ralph_Lauren" class="mw-redirect" title="Polo Ralph Lauren">Ralph Lauren</a> and Waterford<sup id="cite_ref-121" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-121">[121]</a></sup> in a warehouse-club setting. Costco claimed that, similar to its main warehouses, it accepted lower margins in return for greater volume with minimal overhead.
</p><p>Over time, the concept was adjusted to include home electronics, some major appliances, office furniture, and a large selection of outdoor furniture and window treatments. Costco also partners with <a href="/wiki/Glentel" title="Glentel">Glentel</a> subsidiary WIRELESS etc. to sell mobile phones and plans in Canada and Wireless Advocates in the US.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (July 2019)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup></p><p>On April 2, 2009, the company announced that it would be abandoning its Costco Home concept, closing the two existing stores in Kirkland, Washington and <a href="/wiki/Tempe,_Arizona" title="Tempe, Arizona">Tempe, Arizona</a> on July 3, 2009, and abandoning plans for a third store on the West Coast.<sup id="cite_ref-122" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-122">[122]</a></sup> The company cited cutbacks in consumer spending on home products and its interest in focusing on its core business as the main reasons.
</p>
</section><h2 class="section-heading" onclick="javascript:mfTempOpenSection(10)"><div class="mw-ui-icon mw-ui-icon-element indicator mw-ui-icon-small mw-ui-icon-flush-left"></div><span class="mw-headline" id="Controversies">Controversies</span><span class="mw-editsection"><a href="/w/index.php?title=Costco&amp;action=edit&amp;section=35" title="Edit section: Controversies" data-section="35" class="mw-ui-icon mw-ui-icon-element mw-ui-icon-wikimedia-edit-base20 edit-page mw-ui-icon-flush-right">Edit</a></span></h2><section class="mf-section-10 collapsible-block" id="mf-section-10">
<p>In 2010, <a href="/wiki/Mercy_for_Animals" title="Mercy for Animals">Mercy for Animals</a> conducted an undercover investigation at Buckeye Veal Farm, a <a href="/wiki/Veal" title="Veal">veal</a> supplier to Costco.<sup id="cite_ref-123" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-123">[123]</a></sup> Immediately following the investigative release, Costco adopted a policy against purchasing veal from producers that use the <a href="/w/index.php?title=Crate-and-chain&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Crate-and-chain (page does not exist)">crate-and-chain</a> production method.<sup id="cite_ref-124" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-124">[124]</a></sup> The case prompted Ohio lawmakers to vote in favor of a veal crate phase-out in the state.<sup id="cite_ref-125" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-125">[125]</a></sup></p><p>In 2012, Mercy for Animals conducted another undercover investigation of a pork supplier to major retailers such as Costco, <a href="/wiki/Walmart" title="Walmart">Walmart</a>, <a href="/wiki/Safeway_Inc." title="Safeway Inc.">Safeway</a>, <a href="/wiki/Kroger" title="Kroger">Kroger</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Kmart" title="Kmart">Kmart</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-126" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-126">[126]</a></sup> Before the public release of the investigation, Costco announced they would begin requiring their pork suppliers to phase out <a href="/wiki/Gestation_crates" class="mw-redirect" title="Gestation crates">gestation crates</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-127" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-127">[127]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-128" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-128">[128]</a></sup></p><p>In 2014, <i><a href="/wiki/The_Guardian" title="The Guardian">The Guardian</a></i> reported that Costco is a client of <a href="/wiki/Charoen_Pokphand_Foods" title="Charoen Pokphand Foods">Charoen Pokphand Foods</a>. Over six months, <i>The Guardian</i> traced down a supply chain from slave ships in Asian waters to leading producers and retailers. Costco has published a statement saying it has had a supplier code of conduct since 1999 which does not allow this practice, and that independent auditors check for violations regularly.<sup id="cite_ref-129" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-129">[129]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-130" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-130">[130]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-131" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-131">[131]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-132" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-132">[132]</a></sup></p><p>In 2015, <a href="/wiki/The_Humane_Society_of_the_United_States" class="mw-redirect" title="The Humane Society of the United States">The Humane Society of the United States</a> conducted an undercover investigation at an egg supplier to Costco.<sup id="cite_ref-133" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-133">[133]</a></sup> An undercover worker at Hillandale Farms, a major egg supplier to Costco, filmed conditions in which egg-laying hens lived in <a href="/wiki/Battery_cage" title="Battery cage">tiny, wire cages.</a> <sup id="cite_ref-134" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-134">[134]</a></sup> Following the investigations, several celebrities including <a href="/wiki/Brad_Pitt" title="Brad Pitt">Brad Pitt</a> and <a href="/wiki/Ryan_Gosling" title="Ryan Gosling">Ryan Gosling</a> publicly wrote to Costco to address this issue.<sup id="cite_ref-135" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-135">[135]</a></sup> Following efforts by animal protection nonprofits including <a href="/wiki/The_Humane_League" title="The Humane League">The Humane League</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-136" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-136">[136]</a></sup> Costco released an updated commitment to source exclusively cage-free eggs in its operations.<sup id="cite_ref-137" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-137">[137]</a></sup></p><p>In 2016, a follow up to Costco's shift to cage-free eggs by animal rights group <a href="/wiki/Direct_Action_Everywhere" title="Direct Action Everywhere">Direct Action Everywhere</a> (DxE) reported cannibalism and high mortality at a cage-free Costco egg supplier.<sup id="cite_ref-NYT_cage-free_138-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-NYT_cage-free-138">[138]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-139" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-139">[139]</a></sup> Costco denied the allegations, but the video sparked a discussion about animal welfare problems continuing to exist at cage-free egg farms.<sup id="cite_ref-NYT_cage-free_138-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-NYT_cage-free-138">[138]</a></sup> Writing in <i><a href="/wiki/The_Huffington_Post" class="mw-redirect" title="The Huffington Post">The Huffington Post</a></i>, DxE co-founder <a href="/wiki/Wayne_Hsiung" title="Wayne Hsiung">Wayne Hsiung</a> argued that the new investigation, rather than suggesting that Costco should keep birds in cages, indicated that hens should have the right not to be raised for food or kept on farms at all.<sup id="cite_ref-140" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-140">[140]</a></sup></p><p>In August 2017, a federal judge ordered a "deceptive" Costco to pay <a href="/wiki/Tiffany_%26_Co." title="Tiffany &amp; Co.">Tiffany &amp; Co.</a> $19.4<span class="nowrap"> </span>million for misleading consumers into thinking they could buy legitimate Tiffany merchandise at warehouse club prices.<sup id="cite_ref-141" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-141">[141]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-142" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-142">[142]</a></sup></p><p>Costco was criticised in 2019 by the <a href="/wiki/Natural_Resources_Defense_Council" title="Natural Resources Defense Council">Natural Resources Defense Council</a> and <a href="/wiki/SumOfUs" title="SumOfUs">Sumofus</a> for using virgin Canadian <a href="/wiki/Boreal_forest_of_Canada" title="Boreal forest of Canada">boreal forest</a> to make its toilet paper. NRDC says that over the last twenty years, 28 million acres of Canadian boreal forest have been cut down to make toilet paper.<sup id="cite_ref-143" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-143">[143]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-144" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-144">[144]</a></sup></p>
</section><h2 class="section-heading" onclick="javascript:mfTempOpenSection(11)"><div class="mw-ui-icon mw-ui-icon-element indicator mw-ui-icon-small mw-ui-icon-flush-left"></div><span class="mw-headline" id="See_also">See also</span><span class="mw-editsection"><a href="/w/index.php?title=Costco&amp;action=edit&amp;section=36" title="Edit section: See also" data-section="36" class="mw-ui-icon mw-ui-icon-element mw-ui-icon-wikimedia-edit-base20 edit-page mw-ui-icon-flush-right">Edit</a></span></h2><section class="mf-section-11 collapsible-block" id="mf-section-11">
<style data-mw-deduplicate="TemplateStyles:r936637989">.mw-parser-output .portal{border:solid #aaa 1px;padding:0}.mw-parser-output .portal.tleft{margin:0.5em 1em 0.5em 0}.mw-parser-output .portal.tright{margin:0.5em 0 0.5em 1em}.mw-parser-output .portal>ul{display:table;box-sizing:border-box;padding:0.1em;max-width:175px;background:#f9f9f9;font-size:85%;line-height:110%;font-style:italic;font-weight:bold}.mw-parser-output .portal>ul>li{display:table-row}.mw-parser-output .portal>ul>li>span:first-child{display:table-cell;padding:0.2em;vertical-align:middle;text-align:center}.mw-parser-output .portal>ul>li>span:last-child{display:table-cell;padding:0.2em 0.2em 0.2em 0.3em;vertical-align:middle}</style><div role="navigation" aria-label="Portals" class="noprint portal plainlist tright">
<ul><li><span><noscript><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2a/Industry5.svg/28px-Industry5.svg.png" decoding="async" width="28" height="28" class="noviewer" data-file-width="512" data-file-height="512"></noscript><span class="lazy-image-placeholder" style="width: 28px;height: 28px;" data-src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2a/Industry5.svg/28px-Industry5.svg.png" data-alt="" data-width="28" data-height="28" data-srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2a/Industry5.svg/42px-Industry5.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2a/Industry5.svg/56px-Industry5.svg.png 2x" data-class="noviewer"> </span></span><span><a href="/wiki/Portal:Companies" title="Portal:Companies">Companies portal</a></span></li></ul></div>
<ul><li><a href="/wiki/Bulk_foods" title="Bulk foods">Bulk foods</a></li></ul></section><h2 class="section-heading" onclick="javascript:mfTempOpenSection(12)"><div class="mw-ui-icon mw-ui-icon-element indicator mw-ui-icon-small mw-ui-icon-flush-left"></div><span class="mw-headline" id="References">References</span><span class="mw-editsection"><a href="/w/index.php?title=Costco&amp;action=edit&amp;section=37" title="Edit section: References" data-section="37" class="mw-ui-icon mw-ui-icon-element mw-ui-icon-wikimedia-edit-base20 edit-page mw-ui-icon-flush-right">Edit</a></span></h2><section class="mf-section-12 collapsible-block" id="mf-section-12">
